рдкреНрд░ + рдЪреБрджреН + рдгрд┐рдЪреН рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ + рд╢рдкреН рдЕрдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ рдкрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН + [рд▓реЗрдЯреН тЖТ рдЖрдЯреН + рддрд┐рдкреН рдЕрдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ рдкрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН]ред

рдкреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдВ рддрд┐рдЩрдиреНрддрд╕реНрдпреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНред рддрдЪреНрдЪ рдпрддреНрдХрд╛рд░рд╕рджреНрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреНред

реи. рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН (рдкреБ. реирео)

режрем рд╢реНрд░реА-рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ...{Loading}...
рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН-рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрдпрдГ

The celebrated shrI sUkta has spread widely beyond its original role in the vedic gR^ihya liturgy and prayoga-s of the vedic vidhAna-s. Its earliest occurrences are seen in the khila of the R^igveda and the bodhAyana and vaikhAnasa mantra pATha-s of the kR^iShNa yajur veda. It is also related to the ShaShThI sUkta of the mAnava gR^ihya sUtra. The tantric literature also mentions itтАФthe most prominent mention is in the lakShmI tantra (LT 36.121-140 and LT 50.1-237). LT50.1-2367 gives a detailed account of the pA~ncharatric prayoga of the shrI sUkta in worshiping lakShmI. The lakShmI-ratna kosha is another text providing its deployment in the worship of shrI. In the kAdividyA stream of shrI-kula tradition a saMpuTikaraNa of the sUkta and the pa~nchadashI (and other bIja-s like mAya, shrI, kAma, vANI and tripurashekharAnta) is a favored mode of deployment. The shrI sUkta has even been retained by the bauddha nAstika-s and this tradition was until recently alive in Nepal and Bhutan.

The pure vedic form of both the yajurvedic and R^igvedic traditions are no longer commonly practiced, especially in South India. Instead, what one has is a vulgate that is widely used in the drAviDa, Andhra and karnATa countries. It may be recited in a pseudo-yajurvedic form without following the rules of yajurvedic phonetics (e.g. hirANyavarNAM harinIM suvarNa тАж instead of the correct yajuSh form: hirANyavarNA{\m+} harinI{\m+} suvarNa тАж as is specified, for example, in the bodhAyana mantra pATha) or in a form typical of R^igvedic recitation.

Original R^ivedic version is often termed the kAshmIra-pATha because it appears to have been retained in those regions.

рджреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рдбрдкрд╛рдардГ

рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрдпрдГ

This pAtha is from the book ‘yAjusha mantra ratnakaram’ in grantha script, re-printed by Sri Krishnamurti Shastrigal.
It’s original print is likely by vaidhika vardhini press from Kumbhakonam.
What you see in this pAtha (as opposed to the more popular patha) is that it doesn’t have multiple anudAttas in a row in the middle of phrases.

Bear it with the days.

рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдХреНрдд-рдорд╣рджреН-рдЖрджрд┐-рд╡рд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╢реН рдЪреЗрддрдиреЛ рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ
тАШрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рдкрд░рдВ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рддреН ’ ( рдХ. рдЙ. рей. резрез) рдЗрддреНрдпреН-рдЖрджрд┐-рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдГ рд╕ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред

рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ— рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рд╛ рд╖реЛрд│рд╢ рдирд╛рд░рд╛рдпрдгрдГ рдкреМрд░реБрд╖рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдВ рддреБ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

90 (916)
Purusa╠г
N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa
16 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh, except triс╣гс╣нubh 16

This is one of the best-known and most influential hymns of the R╠еgveda. Its central symbol is the p├║ruс╣гa, the тАЬman,тАЭ тАЬperson,тАЭ or тАЬhuman being.тАЭ

On the surface, this hymn tells of the sacrifice of a giant man, from whose parts the world was created. The theme of creation through a cosmic sacrifice is widespread, but this hymn is not simply the retelling of an ancient tradition. The p├║ruс╣гa here serves as a symbol of the sacrifice itself, which especially in the middle Vedic tradition is a locus of creative power. The p├║ruс╣гa is thus similar to the later divine figure Praj─Бpati, who in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas personifies the sacrifice.

Indeed this late hymn represents a verse commentary on the sacrifice that prefigures the prose commentaries of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.+++(5)+++

This hymn is also notable because it is the only R╠еgvedic mention of the four varс╣Зas, the hierarchical division of the social order that forms the theoretical basis for the caste system. One reason that the hymn may have been included in the R╠еgveda to provide a R╠еgvedic charter for such a division of society.

The identity of the Man and the sacrifice is established in the opening verse, for his thousand heads, eyes, and feet recall Agni, the sacrificial fire, and his macro cosmic equivalent, the Sun (cf. Brown 1931: 109тАУ10). The Man comprehends the earth and extends beyond it. As Mus (1968: 549) has pointed out, the тАЬten-fingersтАЩ breadthтАЭ by which he exceeds the world measures from the ManтАЩs hairline to his mouth.+++(4)+++ The ManтАЩs mouth represents speech, which marks the boundary between the imperceptible world of thought and the perceptible world created by speech.+++(5)+++

His mouth is also associated with eating, and in verse 2 the Man rises beyond the world тАЬthrough food,тАЭ that is, by making the world his food. In later texts the тАЬeaterтАЭ is the master and the тАЬeatenтАЭ is one who benefits the master (cf. Rau 1957: 34тАУ35). The image may therefore reflect the ManтАЩs dominance over the world.+++(4)+++ See also X.125, in which the mouth is similarly both the locus of speech and the locus of eating.

This theme of dominance or rule continues also in verse 5 in the mutual generation of the Man and the Vir─Бj. The word vir─Б╠Бj can mean either тАЬbrilliantтАЭ or тАЬruling, rule.тАЭ The latter is the more likely sense here, and therefore this word connects the hymn to Vedic ideals of the king, who in his consecration encompasses the world in a similar way that the Man does here (Proferes 2007: esp. ch. 3). Since the term vir─Б╠Бj is grammatically feminine, it complements p├║ruс╣гa, which is masculine in grammar and connotation.+++(4)+++

The Man is the тАЬofferingтАЭ (vs. 6), the sacrificial victim (vs. 15), but more especially he is the sacrifice itself that the gods, the S─Бdhyas, and seers performed (vs. 7). Through this sacrifice the elements of subsequent sacrifices emerged: the тАЬclotted-mixtureтАЭ (vs. 8), the verses, chants, meters, and sacrificial formulae (vs. 9), and the sacrificial animals (vs. 10). The parts of the sacrifice also became the three upper varс╣Зas (vss. 11тАУ12): his mouth the brahmins, masters of knowledge and speech; his arms the rulers, the possessors of power; and his thighs the freemen or clansmen, who are the productive support of society. These three classes form parts of the sacrifice because they can participate in the sacrifice. The ┼Ы┼лdras or тАЬservantsтАЭ are not part of the sacrifice but rather emerge from the feet of the Man, a symbol of their low social status and their exclusion from the sacrifice. Finally, the elements of the cosmos and gods themselves come forth from the sacrifice (vss. 13тАУ14). This primeval sacrifice thus establishes the тАЬfirst foundationsтАЭ for the performance of the sacrifice or even for the ritual, social, divine, and visible worlds more generally (vs. 16ab), and it creates access to heaven (16cd).

The identity of the S─Бdhyas (in vss. 7 and 16) is not clear. Their name means тАЬthose to be brought to success,тАЭ and they appear to be ancient sacrificers whose proper ritual performance has тАЬperfectedтАЭ them and who have attained god-like status or the status of gods.+++(4)+++

рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рд╕рдорд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░реВрдкреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрджреЗрд╣реЛ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдбрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЛ рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ рд╕реЛрд╜рдпрдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рд╛ ред рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрдирдиреНрддреИрдГ рд╢рд┐рд░реЛрднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╢рд┐рд░рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рддрджреНрджреЗрд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГрдкрд╛рддрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрддрджреАрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдкрд╛рджрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ ред рд╕рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрдЧреЛрд▓рдХрд░реВрдкрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╡реГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрдп рджрд╢рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреБрд▓рдВ рджрд╢рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреБрд▓рдкрд░рд┐рдорд┐рддрдВ рджреЗрд╢рдореН рдЕрддреНрдпрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреН рдЕрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдГ ред рджрд╢рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреБрд▓рдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрд╛рджреНрдмрд╣рд┐рд░рдкрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPuruс╣гa, who has a thousand heads, a thousand eyes, a thousand feet, investing the earth in alldirections, exceeds (it by a space) measuring ten fingers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Puruс╣гa = embodied spirit; or, vir─Бj, the aggregate ofall living beings, spirit embodied in the egg of Brahm─Б, i.e., the universal spirit animating all creation. Thousand= an infinite number; the human soul, extending from the navel, takes upits abode in the heart or the humanbreast; the supreme soul, having animated the universe, is present in man, either in a minute form or of definitedimensions

Jamison Brereton

The Man has a thousand heads, a thousand eyes, and a thousand feet. Having covered the earth on all sides, he extended ten fingersтАЩ breadth beyond.

Griffith

A THOUSAND heads hath Purusa, a thousand eyes, a thousand feet.
On every side pervading earth he fills a space ten fingers wide.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPuruс╣гa is verily all this (visible world), all that is, and all that is to be; he is also the lord of immortality;for he mounts beyond (his own condition) for the food (of living beings).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He mounts: liс╣н, since he rises beyond byfood; or, he is that which grows by nourishment; or, that which expands by nourshment;

Annena = pr─Бс╣Зin─Бmbhoghen─Бnnena nimittabh┼лtena; “inasmuch as he assumes the condition of the world in order that sentientbeings may enjoy the fruit of their acts (pr─Бс╣Зin─Бm karmaphalabhog─Бya), that is not his true nature”: thesupreme spirit, which in its own state is inert and undiscernible, becomes the visible world, that living beings mayreap the fruit of their acts since they acquire mokс╣гa or final liberation, the supreme spirit is the lord of immortality;

Anna = matter (Muс╣Зс╕Нaka Upaniс╣гad 1.8

Jamison Brereton

The Man alone is this whole (world): what has come into being and what is to be.
Moreover, he is master of immortality when he climbs beyond (this
world) through food.

Griffith

This Purusa is all that yet hath been and all that is to be;
The Lord of Immortality which waxes greater still by food.

Geldner

Purusa allein ist diese ganze Welt, die vergangene und die zuk├╝nftige, und er ist der Herr ├╝ber die Unsterblichkeit und auch ├╝ber das, was durch Speise noch weiter w├дchst.

Grassmann

Der Urmensch ist alles dies, was gewesen ist, und was sein wird; er gebietet ├╝ber das Unsterbliche, was durch Speise [Opferspeise] noch h├╢her w├дchst [herrlicher wird].

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSuch is his greatness; and Puruс╣гa is greater even than this; all beings are one-fourth of him; his otherthree-fourths, (being) immortal, (abide) in heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Such is his greatness: i.e., the greatness of Puruс╣гa is as vastas the world of past, present, and future beings

Jamison Brereton

So much is his greatness, but the Man is more than this:
a quarter of him is all living beings; three quarters are the immortal in heaven.

Griffith

So mighty is his greatness; yea, greater than this is Purusa.
All creatures are one-fourth of him, three-fourths eternal life in heaven.

Geldner

Solches ist seine Gr├╢├Яe und noch gewaltiger als dies ist Purusa. Ein Viertel von ihm sind alle Gesch├╢pfe, drei Viertel von ihm ist das Unsterbliche im Himmel.

Grassmann

So bedeutend ist seine Gr├╢sse, und noch gr├╢sser ist der Urmensch; ein Viertel von ihm sind alle Gesch├╢pfe, und drei Viertel von ihm die Welt der Unsterblichen im Himmel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThree-fourths of Puruс╣гa ascended; the other fourth that remained in this world proceeds repeatedly,and, diversified in various forms, went to all animate and inanimate creation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proceeds repeatedly: either inindividuals by death and birth, or in the world by its temporary dissolution and renovation;

S─Б┼Ыan─Бna┼Ыane =those who eat and those who do not; i.e., the two classes of created things, those capable of enjoyment etc., asgods, men, animals, or incapable thereof, as mountains and rivers – conscious and unconscious creation

Jamison Brereton

With his three quarters the Man went upward, but a quarter of him came to be here again.
From there he strode out in different directions toward what eats and what does not eat.

Griffith

With three-fourths Purusa went up: onefourth of him again was here.
Thence he strode out to every side over what cats not and what cats.

Geldner

Zu drei Vierteln stieg Purusa empor, ein Viertel von ihm verj├╝ngte sich hienieden. Von dem aus ging er nach allen Seiten auseinander und erstreckte sich ├╝ber alles was Speise i├Яt und was nicht i├Яt.

Grassmann

Mit drei Vierteln ging der Urmensch oben hinauf, ein Viertel von ihm erschien wieder hier, dann verbreitete er sich ├╝ber alles, was Speise geniesst, und was sie nicht geniesst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFrom him was born Vir─Бt. and from Vir─Бt. Puruс╣гa;
he, as soon as born, became manifested,
and afterwards (created) the earth (and) then corporeal forms.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

From him: tasm─Бt = from that one-fourth; or, from the spirit who by his delusion created the body of Vir─Бс╣н, i.e., the egg of Brahma and entered into it in the form oflife

Jamison Brereton

From him the Vir─Бj was born; from the Vir─Бj the Man.
Upon his birth, he reached beyond the earth from behind and also from in front.

Griffith

From him Viraj was born;
again Purusa from Viraj was born.
As soon as he was born he spread eastward and westward o’er the earth.

Geldner

Aus ihm ward die Viraj geboren, aus der Viraj der Purusa. Geboren ragte er hinten und vorn ├╝ber die Erde hinaus.

Grassmann

Von ihm ward der Allherrscher [vir├вj] geboren und vom Allherrscher der Urmensch. Als er geboren war ├╝berragte er die Erde von hinten und von vorn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the gods performed the sacrifice with Puruс╣гa as the offering, then Spring was its gh─л, Summerthe fuel, and Autumn the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Apparently a reference to an imaginary sacrifice (m─Бnasam)

Jamison Brereton

When, with the Man as the offering, the gods extended the sacrifice, spring was its melted butter, summer its firewood, autumn its offering.

Griffith

When Gods prepared the sacrifice with Purusa as their offering,
Its oil was spring, the holy gift was autumn; summer was the wood.

Geldner

Als die G├╢tter mit Purusa das Opfer vollzogen, da war der Fr├╝hling dessen Schmelzbutter, der Sommer das Brennholz, der Herbst die Opfergabe.

Grassmann

Als die G├╢tter ihr Opfer mit dem Urmenschen als dem Opfertrank kunstvoll bereiteten, da war der Fr├╝hling sein Opferschmalz, der Sommer sein Brennholz, der Herbst sein Opfertrank.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд╛рдВрдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рдХрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдЫрдиреНрджрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрдпрдГ рдЖрд╕рдиреН ред рдРрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрдп рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╡реЗрджрд┐рдХрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдп рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордГ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирд┐рдзрд┐рд░реВрдкрдГ ред рдЕрдд рдПрд╡рд╛рдореНрдирд╛рдпрддреЗ– рди рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреНрдкрд░рд┐ рджрдзрд╛рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рд╣реНрдпреЗрд╡реЛрджреНрдпрдиреН рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВрд╕реНрдпрдкрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐’ (рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. реи.рем.рем.рей) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрдд рдПрдд рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╕рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдкрд░рд┐рдзрдпреЛрд╜рддреНрд░ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдЫрдиреНрджреЛрд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рдорд┐рдзрдГ рддреНрд░рд┐рдГ рд╕рдкреНрдд рддреНрд░рд┐рдЧреБрдгреАрдХреГрддрд╕рдкреНрддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рдПрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рдГ рдХреГрддрд╛рдГ ред рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢ рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд░реНрддрд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдп рдЗрдореЗ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛ рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдп рдПрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рдГ ( рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. рел.рез.резреж.рей) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд╛рдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдПрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рджрд╛рд░реБрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрдзреНрдорддреНрд╡реЗрди рднрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдГред рдпрддреН рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡реИрд░рд╛рдЬреЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдорд╛рдирд╕рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд╛рдГ рдкрд╢реБрдореН рдЕрдмрдзреНрдирдиреН рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЯреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдореЗрд╡ рдкрд╢реБрддреНрд╡реЗрди рднрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдПрддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд░реЗрддреНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ тАШ рдпрддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЗрдг рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSeven were the enclosures of the sacrifice, thrice seven logs of fuel were prepared, when the gods,celebrating the rite, bound Puruс╣гa as the victim.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven enclosures: sapta paridhayaс╕е = seven metres, ga-yatr─лetc., and also as meaning the shallow trenches, three of which were dug round the ─Аhavan─лya fireplace, threeround the northern altar, and the seven ideally dug round the sun to keep off evil spirits. paridhayaс╕е = moats; or,the seven oceans; thrice seven pieces of fuel = twelve months of the year, the five seasons, the three worlds andthe sun; or the three classes of seven metres eaach: Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 5.1.10.3

Jamison Brereton

Its enclosing sticks were seven; the kindling sticks were made three times seven,
when the gods, extending the sacrifice, bound the Man as the
(sacrificial) animal.

Griffith

Seven fencing-sticks had he, thrice seven layers of fuel were prepared,
When the Gods, offering sacrifice, bound, as their victim, Purusa.

Geldner

Ihn besprengten, weihten sie als Opfer auf dem Barhis, den am Anfang geborenen Purusa. Diesen brachten die G├╢tter, die Sadhya┬┤s und die Rishi┬┤s sich zum Opfer.

Grassmann

Diesen zuerst geborenen Urmenschen benetzten sie als ihr Opfer auf der heiligen Streu; durch ihn opferten die G├╢tter die S─Бdhja’s [die zu gewinnenden] und die Rischi’s.

Elizarenkova

With him the gods sacrificed, (also) the S─Бdhyas and those who
were seers.

With him the Deities and all Sadhyas and Rsis sacrificed.

рдЙрд╡рдЯрдГ

English translation:

тАЬFrom that victim, in whom the universal oblation was offered, the mixture of curds and butter was produced, (then) he made those animals over whom V─Бyu presides, those that are wild, and those that aretame.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

V─Бyu: v─Бyuvyan: Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.2.1.3; or, who are governed by instrumental nct

Jamison Brereton

From that sacrifice, when it was offered in full, the clotted-butter mixture was collected.
It [=the sacrifice] was made into the animals: those of the air (and both) those that belong to the wilderness and those that belong to the village.

Griffith

From that great general sacrifice the dripping fat was gathered up.
He formed the creatures of-the air, and animals both wild and tame.

Geldner

Aus diesem vollst├дndig geopferten Opfer entstanden die Verse und Sangesweisen, aus ihm entstanden die Metren, aus ihm entstand der Opferspruch.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFrom that victim, in whom the universal oblation was offered, the с╣Ыccas and s─Бmans were produced;from him the metres were born; from him the yajus. was born.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tasm─Бd yaj├▒─Бt = from that simple portionsurnamed the universal sacrifice, sarvah┼лtaс╕е, meaning Puruс╣гa as the world;

Yaj├▒a = yaj├▒as─Бdhana, thematerial of sacrifice, i.e., the victim. Puruс╣гa is the spiritual cause and effect of material creation; it is from him,not from the ideal or real sacrifice, that all things originate\

Jamison Brereton

From this sacrifice, when it was offered in full, the verses and chants were born.
Meters were born from it. The sacrificial formulaтАФfrom it that was born.

Griffith

From that great general sacrifice Rcas and Sama-hymns were born:
Therefrom were spells and charms produced; the Yajus had its birth from it.

Geldner

Aus ihm entstanden die Rosse und alle Tiere mit doppelter Zahnreihe, aus ihm entstanden die Rinder, aus ihm sind die Ziegen und Schafe entstanden.

Grassmann

Aus ihm entsprangen die Rosse und alle mit zwei Zahnreihen versehenen Thiere; aus ihm entsprangen die Rinder, aus ihm die Ziegen und Schafe.

Elizarenkova

From it horses were born and whatever animals have teeth in both jaws. Cows were born from it. From it were born goats and sheep.

From it were horses born, from it all cattle with two rows of teeth:
From it were generated kine, from it the goats and sheep were born.

English translation:

тАЬWhen they immolated Puruс╣гa, into how many portions did they divide him? What was his mouth called, what his arms, what his thighs, what were his feet called?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When they apportioned the Man, into how many parts did they arrange him?
What was his mouth? What his two arms? What are said to be his two thighs, his two feet?

Griffith

When they divided Purusa how many portions did they make?
What do they call his mouth, his arms? What do they call his thighs and feet?

Geldner

Sein Mund ward zum Brahmanen, seine beiden Arme wurden zum Rajanya gemacht, seine beiden Schenkel zum Vaisya, aus seinen F├╝├Яen entstand der Sudra.

Grassmann

Sein Mund ward zum Brahmanen, seine Arme zum R─Бdschanja, seine Schenkel zum Vai├зja, aus seinen F├╝ssen entsprang der ├З┼лdra.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHis mouth became the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, his arms became the R─Бjanya, his thighs became the Vai┼Ыya;the ┼Ъ┼лdra was born from his feet.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Br─Бhmaс╣Зa was his mouth; the R─Бjanya was made his arms; thatwhich was the Vai┼Ыya was his thighs; the S’┼кdra sprang from his feet: Muir, Sanskrit Texts, vol. 1, p.9

Jamison Brereton

The brahmin was his mouth. The ruler was made his two arms.
As to his thighsтАФthat is what the freeman was. From his two feet the servant was born.

Griffith

The Brahman was his mouth, of both his arms was the Rajanya made.
His thighs became the Vaisya, from his feet the Sudra was produced.

Geldner

Der Mond ist aus seinem Geist entstanden, die Sonne entstand aus seinem Auge; aus seinem Munde Indra und Agni, aus seinem Aushauch entstand der Wind.

Grassmann

Aus seinem Geiste entsprang der Mond, aus seinem Auge die Sonne, aus seinem Munde Indra und Agni, aus seinem Athem der Wind.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe moon was born from his mind; the sun was born from his eye; Indra and Agni were born from his mouth, V─Бyu from his breath.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, air and breath proceeded from his ear and fire rose from his mouth: Yajuс╣г

Jamison Brereton

The moon was born from his mind. From his eye the sun was born. From his mouth Indra and Agni, from his breath V─Бyu was born.

Griffith

The Moon was gendered from his mind, and from his eye the Sun had birth;
Indra and Agni from his mouth were born, and Vayu from his breath.

Geldner

Aus dem Nabel ward der Luftraum, aus dem Haupte ging der Himmel hervor, aus den F├╝├Яen die Erde, aus dem Ohre die Weltgegenden. So regelten sie die Welten.

Grassmann

Aus seinem Nabel ward die Luft, aus seinem Kopf entstand der Himmel, aus seinen F├╝ssen die Erde, aus seinem Ohr die Weltgegenden; so bildeten sie die Welten.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬFrom his navel came the firmament, from his head the heaven was produced, the earth from his feet,the quarters of space from his ear, so they constituted the world.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From his navel was the midspace. From his head the heaven developed. From his two feet the earth, and the directions from his ear. Thus they arranged the worlds.

Griffith

Forth from his navel came mid-air the sky was fashioned from his head
Earth from his feet, and from his car the regions. Thus they formed the worlds.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy sacrifice the gods worshipped (him who is also) the sacrifice; those were the first duties. Those great ones became partakers of the heaven where the ancient deities the S─Бdhyas abide. тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With the sacrifice the gods performed the sacrifice for themselves: these were the first foundations.
These, its greatness, accompanied (it) to heavenтАЩs vault,
where the ancient S─Бdhyas and the gods are.

Whitney
Translation
  1. By the sacrifice the gods sacrificed to the sacrifice; those were
    the first ordinances (dh├бrman); those greatnesses attach themselves to
    (sac) the firmament, where are the ancient (p┼л╠Бrva) perfectible
    (s─Бdhy├б) gods.
Notes

The verse is RV. i. 164. 50,* found also in VS. (xxxi. 16), TS. (iii. 5. 11тБ╡), TA. (iii. 12. 7), MS. (iv. 10. 3), CB. (x. 2. 2┬│, with
comment); тМКKaс╣нha-hss., p. 83;тМЛ the only variant is sacante for
sacanta in TS.TA.

“This passage and vii. 79. 2 cast light upon the idea of s─Бdhya; there are two kinds of gods:

  • those with Indra at their head and
  • the s─Бdhya ’they who are to be won’ (s─Бdhya ‘what is to be
    brought into order, under control, or into comprehension’).

They are thus the unknown, conceived as preceding the known. Later they are worked into the ordinary classification of Vasus, Rudras, etc.; and what was formerly a serious religious problem, a hierarchy conceived as possible before the now-accepted gods (something like the pre-Olympians with the Greeks), has become an empty name.”

R. *тМКAlso RV. x. 90. 16.тМЛ

Griffith

Gods, sacrificing, sacrificed the victim these were the earliest holy ordinances.
The Mighty Ones attained the height of heaven, there where the Sidhyas, Gods of old, are dwelling.

Griffith - AV

The Gods adored the Sacrifice with worship: these were the statutes of primeval ages. Those mighty ones attained the cope of heaven, there where the Sadhyas, Gods of old, are dwelling.

Geldner

Mit dem Opfer opferten die G├╢tter dem Opfer. Dies waren die ersten Normen des Opfers. Diese M├дchte schlossen sich dem Himmel an, in dem die fr├╝heren G├╢tter, die Sadhya┬┤s, sich befinden.

Grassmann

Durch Opfer opferten die G├╢tter das Opfer; das waren die ersten Br├дuche; sie, die erhabenen, gelangten zum Gipfel des Himmels, wo die alten zu gewinnenden [s─Бdhy─Бs] G├╢tter sind.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEarnetly I glorify the exploits of Viс╣гс╣Зu, who made the three worlds; who sustained the lofty aggregate site (of the spheres); thrice traversing (the whole); who is praised by the exalted.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P─Бrthiv─Бni vimame raj─Бс╣Гsi = lit. he made the earthly regions;

Pс╣Ыthiv─л = three worlds: atra trayo lok─Б api pс╣Ыthiv─л ┼Ыabdav─Бcy─Б; Indra and Agni are said to abide in the lower, middle and upper pс╣Ыthiv─л or world– yad indr─Бgn─л avamasy─Бm pс╣Ыth─лvy─Бm madhyamasy─Бm paramasyam uta stha (RV. 1.108.9; Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.2.12.1); seven lower lok─Бs are also included in the word pс╣Ыthiv─л;or, the term is limited to the three regions addressed in prayer, bh┼лс╕е bhuvar svar; who sustained the lofty: uttaram sadhastham askabh─Бyat: sadastha = the firmament, as the asylum of the three regions– lokatray─Б┼Ыrayabh┼лtam antarikс╣гam; or, the seven regions above the earth; or, the highest region of all, whence there is no return; or the above of the righteous, the satya-loka;

Askabh─Бyat = nirmitav─Бn, created; thrice traversing: vicakram─Бс╣Зas tredh─Б (idam viс╣гс╣Зurvi cakrame: RV. 1.22.17); traversing in various ways in own created worlds

Jamison Brereton

Now shall I proclaim the heroic deeds of Viс╣гс╣Зu, who measured out the earthly realms,
who propped up the higher seat, having stridden out three times, the wide-ranging one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn begins with an almost exact echo of the famous opening p─Бda of the Indra hymn I.32 ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├б vocam. In place of ├нndrasya we have v├нс╣гс╣Зoс╕е and the missing syllable is made up by inserting the fairly functionless particle kam after n├║.

Griffith

I WILL declare the mighty deeds of Visnu, of him who measured out the earthly regions,
Who propped the highest place of congregation, thrice setting down his footstep, widely striding.

Macdonell

I will proclaim the mighty deeds of Viс╣гс╣Зu, Of him who measured out the earthly spaces; Who, firmly propping up the higher station, Strode out in triple regions, widely pacing.

Keith

I shall proclaim the mighty deeds of Visnu
Who meted out the spaces of the earth,
Who established the highest abode,
Stepping thrice, the far-goer.

Grassmann

Des Vischnu grosse Thaten will ich preisen, der weit durchmessen hat der Erde R├дume, Befestigt hat den h├╢chsten Sitz des Himmels, dreimal ausschreitend mit gewalt’gen Schritten.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I attain his favourite path, in which god-seeking men delight; (the path) of that wide-stepping Viс╣гс╣Зu, in whose exalted station there is a (perpetual) flow of felicity; for to such a degree is he the friend (of the pious).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

His favourite path: the firmament: patho anatarikс╣гam

Jamison Brereton

Might I reach that dear cattle-pen of his, where men seeking the gods find elation,
for exactly that is the bond to the wide-striding one: the wellspring of honey in the highest step of Viс╣гс╣Зu.

Griffith

May I attain to that his well-loved mansion where men devoted to the Gods are happy.
For there springs, close akin to the Wide-Strider, the well of meath in Visnu’s highest footstep.

Macdonell

I would attain to that his dear dominion Where men devoted to the gods do revel. In the wide-striding Viс╣гс╣Зu’s highest footstep There is a spring of mead: such is our kinship.

Grassmann

O m├╢cht’ ich seinen lieben Sitz erreichen, in dem die frommen M├дnner selig leben; Denn das sind recht des m├дcht’gen Schreiters Freunde, und S├╝sses quillt an Vischnu’s h├╢chster Fussspur.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu is therefore glorified, that by his prowess he is like a fearful, ravenous, and mountain-haunting wild beast, and because of that in his three paces all worlds abide.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mountain-haunting wild beast: mс╣Ыga or siс╣Гha, a lion, as applicable to Viс╣гс╣Зu: one who seeks for his enemies to inflict punishment on them, and is therefore, fearful and fierce;

Giriс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е = he who dwells on high, or who abides in prayer and the like: mantr─Бdir┼лp─Бy─Бm v─Бci artam─Бnaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

In this way Viс╣гс╣Зu will be praised for his heroic deedтАФ(he who is) like a fearsome wild beast, living in the mountains and roaming wherever it wants,
in whose three wide strides dwell all living beings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The covert identification with Indra continues in p─Бda b, which is identical to X.180.2a, where Indra is the referent.

Griffith

For this his mighty deed is Visnu lauded, like some wild beast, dread, prowling, mountain-roaming;
He within whose three wide-extended paces all living creatures have their habitation.

Macdonell

Because of this his mighty deed is Viс╣гс╣Зu Lauded, like some fierce beast that is much dreaded, That wanders as it lists, that haunts the mountains: He in whose three wide strides abide all creatures.

Geldner

Also wird Vishnu ob seiner Heldentat gepriesen, der umherschweifend im Gebirge haust wie das furchtbare wilde Tier, in dessen drei weiten Schritten alle Gesch├╢pfe Wohnung finden.

Grassmann

Ger├╝hmt wird Vischnu wegen dieser Grossthat, gleich wildem L├╢wen, der durch Berge schweifet, Er, unter dessen drei gewalt’gen Schritten die Wesen alle sichre Wohnung haben.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExpanding with a body beyond all measure, Viс╣гс╣Зu men comprehend not your magnitude; we knowthese your two worlds (computing) from the earth, but you, divine Viс╣гс╣Зu, are cognisant of the highest.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your twoworlds: i.e. the earth and the firmament, which are visible; cf. RV. 10.082.05

Jamison Brereton

O you who have grown with your body beyond measure, they do not attain to your greatness.
We (only) know both your dusky realms of the earth; god Viс╣гс╣Зu, you yourself know the farthest one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Renou supplies тАЬother godsтАЭ as the subj. of ├бnv a┼Ыnuvanti in b. This seems perfectly acceptable, though not strictly necessary. And since in vs. 2 it is, presumably, mortals (since they are тАШbornтАЩ) who fail to reach the limit of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs greatness, mortals could also be the subject here. See remarks below on the formulatic connection between the two vss.

As Renou points out, both the case of the complement (acc. versus gen.) and the voice (act. versus mid.) differ between 1st pl. vidma in c and 2nd sg. vitse in d. The middle voice of vitse makes sense, since Viс╣гс╣Зu knows his own farthest realm; the variation in case is harder to account for. Perhaps the two earthly realms are subjects of direct knowledge, while the farthest realm is something even Viс╣гс╣Зu only knows of.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The b-p─Бdas of these two vss. are variants of each other, using two different roots for тАШattainтАЩ (тИЪna┼Ы, тИЪ─Бp) and two different formulations of тАШgreatnessтАЩ, the 2nd an elaboration on the first: 1b n├б te mahitv├бm ├бnv a┼Ыnuvanti 2ab n├б te тАж mahimn├бс╕е p├бram ├бntam ─Бpa Another example of the freedom of RVic formulaics; see comm. ad VII.98.5 in the previous hymn for further on this.

Griffith

MEN come not nigh thy majesty who growest beyond all bound and measure with thy body.
Both thy two regions of the earth, O Visnu, we know: thou God, knowest the highest also.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Viс╣гс╣Зu traversed the earth for a dwelling which he was desirous of giving to his eulogist; firm arethe people who are his praisers; he who is the engenderer of good has made a spacious dwelling (for hisworshippers).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which he was desirous of giving: manuс╣гe da┼Ыasyan = stuvate devagaс╣З─Бya, to the company ofgods praising him– Viс╣гс╣Зu having taken the three worlds from the Asuras to give to them; the engenderer ofgood: or, to whom belong fortunate births

Jamison Brereton

Quick Viс╣гс╣Зu strode across this earth for a dwelling place for Manu, showing his favor.
Firmly fixed are his peoples, (even) the weak. He, affording good birth, has made (them) wide dwelling.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By concentrating Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs strides in the first p─Бda of 4, the poet is free to express the aim of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs action – creating space and dwelling places for the people

– in the rest of the vs. As Geldner points out (n. 4c), asya can refer either to Viс╣гс╣Зu or to Manu, although in actuality this may not matter. It may be an instance of тАЬtrickle-downтАЭ ownership: Viс╣гс╣Зu makes a dwelling place for Manu, and in turn ManuтАЩs people also get firmly planted. Or, Manu and the people may both be under Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs auspices.

03-04 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

Griffith

Over this earth with mighty step strode Visnu, ready to give it for a home to Manu.
In him the humble people trust for safety: he, nobly born, hath made them spacious dwellings.

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

Three times did the quick god stride with his greatness across this earth worth a hundred verses.
Let Viс╣гс╣Зu be preeminent, stronger than the strong, for vibrant is the
name of this stalwart one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Flg. a suggestion by Geldner (n. 3a, though not reflected in his tr.), I take eс╣г├бin p─Бda a (also 4a) as belonging to the stem eс╣г├б- тАШquickтАЩ, which is used several times of Viс╣гс╣Зu in the gen. expression v├нс╣гс╣Зor eс╣г├бsya (II.34.11, VII.40.5, VIII.20.3), in which confusion with the nom. pronominal eс╣г├б(с╕е) (possible here) is excluded.

The hapax ┼Ыat├бrcas- is problematic. The Pp analyses the 2nd member as arcasam, but Wackernagel (AiG I.318) points out that the sandhi between the cmpd members would require rather -с╣Ыcasam. However, Oldenberg disputes this, claiming that it would then have to be written (тАЬтАж geschrieben werden m├╝ssenтАЭ) *┼Ыat├бс╣Ыcasam , though itтАЩs not clear to me why. Interpr. differ significantly: S─Бyaс╣Зa. glosses with arcis-.

Oldenberg posits a masc. s-stem *arc├бs- тАШsingerтАЩ, comparing VI.34.3 y├бdi stot─Б╠Бraс╕е ┼Ыat├бс╣Г y├бt sah├бsraс╣Г gс╣Ыс╣З├бnti тАЬWhen a hundred, when a thousand praisers sing to him тАж,тАЭ an interpr. followed by Geldner – though the connection between the two passages seems tenuous to me. By contrast, Renou tr. тАЬau cent ├йclats,тАЭ perhaps flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs arc├нs-. Since an infinitival dat. с╣Ыc├бse тАШto praise, for chanting (praise)тАЩ is found in VI.39.5 and VII.61.6, it seems reasonable to take the underlying stem с╣Ыcas- as the base here, as Grassmann does, glossing тАШhundertfach zu preisenтАЩ. My тАШworth a hundred versesтАЩ is close to that, though perhaps тАШpraises, chantsтАЩ would be better.

Because of the lack of accent on asya, it should be pronominal, not adjectival; I would adjust the tr. to тАЬof him, the stalwart.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

12рдпрджрд┐рддрд┐ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рее рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдХрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рди рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЛ рд╡рд╛рд╣рдХ рдпрджреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрдкрд┐рддреДрдиреН рдЛрддрд╛рд╡реГрдзрдГ рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреДрдиреН рдпрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдпрдЬрд╕рд┐ ред рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╕рд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рд╕рд┐ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рдкрд┐рддреГрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ ред рдЖрдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреБрднрд╛рд╡рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореЗрд╡ рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрд╛рдо рдЗрддрд┐ рее

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Brahm─Б of the gods, the guide of the sages, the с╣Ыс╣гi of the pious, the buffalo of wild animals, the falcon of the vultures, the hatchet of deadly weapons, the Soma passes through the filter with a roar.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Brahm─Б of the gods: i.e., the king of the gods; or, it may mean the br─Бhmaс╣Зa of the priests; the с╣Ыс╣гi: yaс╕е parokс╣гam pa┼Ыyati sa с╣Ыс╣гiс╕е, с╣Ыsirdar┼Ыan─Бt (Nirukta 2.11)

Jamison Brereton

Formulator for the gods, trail-blazer for the sage poets, seer for the inspired poets, buffalo of the wild beasts,
falcon of the birds of prey, axe of the treesтАФSoma goes rasping
through the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though the syntax is kept absolutely constant - nom. sg. + gen. pl. - there is a shifting functional relationship between the head noun and its genitive in the seven phrases here: the first two are roles Soma performs for the group identified by the gen., the next three a particular, and superior, individual token from the group (though the third pairing, тАЬseer for/of the inspired poets,тАЭ is ambiguous between the first type and the second), and the last is sort of a negative version of the role he plays for the group.

Griffith

Brahman of Gods, the Leader of the poets, Rsi of sages, Bull of savage creatures,
Falcon amid the vultures, Axe of forests, over the cleansing sieve goes Soma singing.

Geldner

Der Hohepriester der G├╢tter, der Pfadfinder der Seher, der Rishi unter den Beredten, der B├╝ffel unter den wilden Tieren, der Adler unter den Geiern, die Axt f├╝r die B├дume, geht Soma laut redend durch die Seihe.

Grassmann

Der G├╢tter Beter und der Priester F├╝hrer, der S├дnger Dichter und der Stier der Thiere, Der Geier Adler und die Axt der W├дlder, der Soma wandert singend durch die Seihe.

Keith

I The gander seated in purity, the bright one seated in the atmosphere,
The Hotr seated at the altar, the guest seated in the house,
Seated among men, seated in the highest, seated in holy order, seated in the firmament, Born of the waters, born of the cows, born of holy order, born of the mountain, the great holy order.
